General Conditions of Admission, Consent, Assignment of Benefits & Financial Agreement

Consent to Diagnostic Tests, Procedures and Medical Treatment: Ido voluntarily consent to hospital care involving diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my treating physician(s), practitioner(s) and his or her designees. This consent includes testing for communicable diseases, including but not limited to Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), hepatitis or any other blood-borne infectious disease if ordered for a diagnostic purpose or due to occupational exposure of a health care worker. I acknowledge no guarantee has been made to me as to the results of examination and treatment in the hospital.

Independent Contractor Acknowledgement:

I understand and acknowledge the physicians and other practitioners involved in my care, including but not limited to my attending physician, consulting physicians, emergency department physicians, physician assistants, nurse practitioners, radiologists, anesthesiologists, nurse anesthetists and pathologists are not agents or employees of The Medical Center. I further understand I will be billed separately for services by these providers. These providers have independent relationships with insurance companies, and the hospital makes no guarantee as to any preferred provider relationships with these physicians/practitioners.

Assignment of Benefits and Financial Agreement:

I certify all information given by me is correct and I accept responsibility for the charges for the care provided. I agree to the assignment of all third-party benefits to The Medical Center and to any physician, practitioner, organization or independent contractor who provided products or services, and agree to pay all charges not covered by

Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice messages and/or automated dialing.

Release of Information:

I authorize the release of all or part of my records, including information stored in The Medical Center corporate-wide database, to my physician(s), whose name I provided at the time of registration, and to any physician or practitioner who has or will provide services to me. I authorize the release of statistical information as required by any local, state or federal agency or managed care program. I authorize the release ‘of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implantable medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the FDA. I authorize the release of my HIV and hepatitis test results to health care personnel in the event of an occupational exposure.

I authorize the hospital, physicians and any other holder of medical or

other information to release any information about me (including medical information concerning psychological or psychiatric conditions,

alcoholism and/or drug related conditions and HIV or other blood-bome infectious diseases) required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on an inpatient or outpatient basis to any person or corporation which is or may be liable for all or part of the total charge incurred, including but not limited to insurance companies, the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and carriers, state agencies and workers’ compensation carriers, as well as the review organization employed by my employer or the employer of the insured member of my family and any corporation engaged by the hospital to make collection of any unpaid hospital charges. I further authorize my employer to

third-party payers. If 1 am covered by an ERISA plan, with this assignment release to the hospital or any agency engaged for the purpose of collecting

I specifically authorize my providers to receive copies of all notifications and information that I am legally entitled to receive under the terms of my insurance/health plan and to act on my behalf to appeal benefit determinations. I acknowledge any claim for benefits from a third party payer may be filed by The Medical Center as a courtesy to me. However, Tam primarily responsible for monitoring the filing process and making

certain the claim is filed in compliance with the provisions specified by. the evaluated as part of this pro; applicable third party payer. The filing of the claim by The Medical Center performance. I understand

in no way absolves me from liability for any portion of the bill not paid by a third party payer for any reason. In the case of outpatient services, I agree this document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically tevoked by me in writing. This writing is intended to be the complete and exclusive statement of the terms and conditions regarding my assignment of benefits and supersedes all previous communications, representations or agreements, whether oral or written. Any terms or conditions proposed by me or on my behalf that differ from or are in addition to the terms of this agreement are rejected and shall not become part of this agreement.

Unless other payment arrangements are approved by The Medical Center, the account balance is due upon demand. Failure to remit payment for the services may result in the placement of an account with a collection agency or attomey for collection. All amounts due, as reflected by the final statement and/or amended final statement, shall bear interest from the due date until paid at a per annum rate of eight percent (8%). In the event a claim is reduced to judgment, it shall accrue interest at the judgment rate of six percent (6%) until paid in full. Further, ] agree to pay all costs of collection including court costs, interest, attorney fees and collection agency fees.

Contact Information:

I agree The Medical Center, Commonwealth Health Corporation and their agents, attorneys or collection agencies may contact me regarding medical information or information about my account or for the purposes of collection by telephone at any number provided by me including wireless telephone numbers, and via text messaging or e-mail to any e-mail address provided. Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice messages and/or automated dialing.

Hospital Quality and Efficiency Program:

Thave been informed that doctors on the medical staff may participate in a program designed to further promote the quality and efficiency of patient care services rendered at The Medical Center. Aspects of my care may be pera and doctors may be paid related to their

at this program will not increase any of my

costs or that of any insurer or governmental payor who helps pay for my care. The program is funded solely by The Medical Center as part of its commitment to provide high quality care to the community. I can opt out of this program and/or learn more about it by contacting [PHONE-142].

WORKERS COMP MEDICAL WAIVER AND CONSENT L Cava Ra having filed a claim for workers’ compensation benefits, do hereby waive any physician-patient, psychiatrist-patient, or chiropractor-patient privilege I may have and hereby authorize any health care provider to furnish to my employer, its workers compensation carrier or its agent, the Division of Workers' Compensation Funds, the Uninsured Employer's Fund, or Administrative Law Judge any information or written material reasonably related to my work-related injury occurring on or about x any medical information relevant to the claim, including past history of complaints of, or treatment of, a condition Similar to that presented in this claim or other conditions related to the same body part.

Such information is being disclosed to the purpose of facilitating my claim for Kentucky workers’ compensation benefits.

I understand that I have the right to revoke this authorization in writing at any time by sending written notification to each individual health care provider, but such revocation will not have any affect on actions taken prior to revocation. Moreover, inasmuch as KRS 342.020(8) requires a medical waiver to be executed, revocation may result in suspension or delay of the workers' compensation claim.

I understand that no medical provider may condition treatment or payment on whether I sign this medical waiver, however, I further understand that failure to sign this medical waiver may result in suspension or delay of the workers' compensation claim.

J understand that the information used or disclosed pursuant to this medical waiver may be subject to re-disclosure by the recipient.

This authorization shall remain valid for 180 days following its execution. A photocopy of the authorization may be accepted in lieu of the

The authorization includes, but is not restricted to, a right to review and obtain all copies of all records, x-rays, x-ray reports, medical charts, prescriptions, diagnoses, opinions and courses of treatment.

KENTUCKY WORKERS' COMPENSATION AND HIPAA

On April 14, 2003, the federal Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act [HIPAA], privacy regulation took effect. This regulation limits the situations in which medical providers may release patient information, unless the information is necessary for the purpose of treatment, payment, or health care operations. Moreover, it is important to note that disclosures for workers' compensation are in most instances exempt from HIPAA privacy requirements. The exact wording is as follows: "A covered entity may disclose protected health information as authorized by and to the extent necessary to comply with laws relating to workers' compensation..."

Since HIPAA defers to state law regarding disclosures relating to workers' compensation, it is important for claimants and medical providers to know what Kentucky law requires for disclosure of patient information. An employee who reports a work injury or who files for workers compensation benefits must "execute a waiver and consent of any physician-patient, psychiatrist-patient, or chiropractor-patient privilege with respect to any condition or complaint reasonably related to the condition for which the employee claims compensation." KRS 342.020 (8). The upper portion of this Form 106 is the waiver and consent that cach employee must sign. Kentucky law further states that once this Form 106 is signed, any health care provider "shall, within a reasonable time after written request by the employee, employer, workers’ compensation insurer for its agent or assignee], special fund, uninsured employers fund, or the administrative law judge, provide the requesting party with any information or written material reasonably related to any injury or disease for which the employee claims compensation."

Once the Form 106 is signed, health care providers may disclose information as set out in Kentucky law. Another section of the regulation allows release of information pursuant to an administrative or judicial order or subpoena, provided that there has been a reasonable effort to notify the injured worker [or his attorney] that such a request has been made. Should there be questions regarding disclosures pursuant to this form, appropriate legal counsel should be consulted or you can contact the Department of Workers' Claims at [PHONE-124].

Workers’ Comp Medical

Promethazine tablets What is this medicine?

PROMETHAZINE (proe METH @ zeen) is an antihistamine. It is used to treat allergic reactions and to treat or prevent nausea and vomiting from illness or motion sickness. It is also used to make you sleep before surgery, and to help treat pain or nausea after surgery.

How should I use this medicine?

Fake this medicine by mouth with a glass of water. Follow the directions on the prescription label. Take your doses at regular intervals. Do not take your medicine more often than directed.

Talk to your pediatrician regarding the use of this medicine in children. Special care may be needed. This medicine should not be given to infants and children younger than 2 years old.

What side effects may 1 notice from receiving this medicine? Side effects that you should report to your dector or health care professianal as soon as possible:

® blurred vision

® irregular heartbeat, palpitations or chest pain ® muscle or facial twitches

® pain or difficulty passing urine

® seizures

® skin rash

® slowed or shallow breathing

®@ unusual bleeding or bruising

® yellowing of the eyes or skin

Side effects that usuaily do not require medical attention (report to your doctor or health care professional if they continue or are bothersome):

® headache

® nightmares, agitation, nervousness, excitability, mot able to sleep (these are more likely in children)

# stuffy nose

What may interact with this medicine?

Do not take this medicine with any of the following medications:

® clsapride

® dofetitide

® dronedarone

® MAOIs fike Carbex, Eldepryl, Marplan, Nardil, Parnate ® pimozide

® quinidine, including dextromethorphan; quinidine

This medicine may also interact with the following medications:

® certain medicines for depression, anxiety, or psychotic disturbances

% certain medicines for anxiety or sleep

® certain medicines for seizures like carbamazepine, phenobarbital, phenytoin

® certain medicines for movement abnormalities as in Parkinson's disease, or for gestrointestinal prablerns

® epinephrine

® medicines for allergies or colds

® muscle relaxants

® narcotic medicines for pain

@ other medicines that prolong the QT interval (cause an abnormal heart rhythm)

® tramadol

* trimethobenzamide

What if I miss a dose?

If you miss a dose, take it as soon as you can. If it is almost time for your next dose, take only that dese. Do not take double or extra doses.

Where should I keep my medicine?

Keep out of the reach of children.

Store at room temperature, between 20 and 25 degrees C (68 and 77 degrees F). Protect from light. Throw away any unused medicine after the expiration date.

What should I teil my health care provider before I take this medicine? They need to know if you have any of these conditions:

® glaucoma

® high blood pressure or heart disease

# kidney disease

® liver disease

® lung or breathing disease, like asthria

® prostate trouble

® pain or difficulty passing urine

* seizures

® an unusual or alergic reaction to promethazine or phenothiazines, other medicines, foods, dyes, or preservatives

® pregnant or trying ta get pregnant

® breast-feeding

What should I watch for while using this medicine?

Tell your doctor or health care professional if your symptorns do not start to get better in 1 to 2 days.

You may gat drowsy or dizzy. Do not drive, use machinery, or do anything that needs mental alertness until you know how this medicine affects you. To reduce the risk of dizzy or fainting spells, do not stand or sit up quickly, especially if you are an older patient. Alcohol may increase dizziness and drowsiness. Avoid alcoholic drinks.

Your mouth may get dry. Chewing sugarless gum or sucking hard candy, and drinking plenty of water may help. Contact your doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe.

This medicine may cause dry eyes and blurred vision. If you wear contact lenses you may feel some discornfort. Lubricating drops may help. See your eye doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe.

This medicine can make you more sensitive to the sun. Keen out of the sun. If you cannot avoid being in the sun, wear protective clothing and use sunscreen. Do not use sun lamps or tanning beds/booths.

If you are diabetic, check your blood-sugar levels regularly.

Norco Oral Tablet 10 mg/325 mg Uses

For pain.

Instructions

This medicine may be taken with or without food.

Keep the medicine at root temperature. Avoid heat and direct light.

To reduce constipation, eat high fiber foods, drink plenty of water and exercise.

Please tell your doctor and pharmacist about all the medicines you take. Include both prescription and over-the-counter medicines. Also tell them about any vitamins, herbal medicines, or anything else you take for your health.

It is very lripertant that you follow your doctor's instructions for all Mood tests.

Do not take more than 6 pills in a day.

Cautions

This medicine contains an opioid. Though it helps rnany people, this medicine may sornetinnes cause addiction, especially if it is used for a long time. This risk for addiction may be higher if you have a substance use disorder - such as overuse of or addiction to drugs or alcohol. Speak with your doctar about the benefits and risks of using this medicine.

Ask your doctor or pharmacist if you should have naloxone on hand to treat opioid overdose. Teach your family or household members about the signs of an opioid overdose and how to treat it.

Tf you stop this medicine suddenty, after using & regularly for a long time, you may have withdrawal symptoms. Your doctor may ask you to slowly reduce your dose before stopping it. Tell your doctor right away if you notice any symptoms of withdrawal. Withdrawal symptorns can include unusual sweating, watering eyes, runny nose, chills, stomach pain, diarrhea, yawning, muscle aches, irritability, restlessness, anxiety, trouble sleeping, or thoughts of suicide.

Tall your doctor and pharmacist if you ever had an allergic reaction to a redicine. Symotorms of an allergic reaction can include trouble breathing, skin rash, itching, swelling, or severe dizziness.

Do not use the medication any more than instructed.

if possible, avoid using with marijuana or other medicines that can cause dizziness or drowsiness. These include allergy/cold products, muscle relaxers, sleep aids, and pain relievers.

Your ability to stay alert or to react quickly may be impaired by this medicine. Do nat operate

Bladder Care after Outpatient Surgery Caring for your Bladder after Outpatient Surgery

Sometimes surgery and anesthesia medicines can affect your bladder for several hours. This information will help you care for your bladder after you are discharged home. The inability to empty your bladder after surgery, a condition called urinary retention, is considered an amergency if you are no longer in the hospital. If you are unable to ernpty your bladder within 6-8 hours frorn the time your surgery ended, you should seek treatrnent from your locat amergency room. This time is am/prm.

How does surgery affect my bladder?

+ Surgery can cause a temporary interruption of nerve impulses from the brain to the bladder, decreasing the sensation and feeling that you need to urinate.

- Temporary swelling after surgery can also affect your ability to empty your bladder.

» When the bladder gets full and can hold no more urine, it can cause stretching of the bladder which can cause damage to the bladder musties. When the bladder can hold no more urine, fluid backs up Inte the kidneys, which can also cause damade.

What can I do if I can't urinate?

* Try running the water in the sink. Sometimes the sound of running water helps.

» Sit ina warm bath or get into the shower (if not contraindicated by your procedure}.

- Fry placing your hands in cold water.

» Walk. Walk. Walk.

- Do not keep drinking large amounts of fluid # you feel tke your bladder is full and you cannot em: ib.

* GO TO YOUR LOCAL EMERGENCY ROOM

Operative Note

Signed Patient: Hall,Cora Mae MR#: LO00617236 DOB: [DOB-1] Acct:L00039407077 Age/Sex: 33 / F ADM Date: 12/08/22 Loc: AMB SURG Attending Dr: Chaitanya S Malempati DO Pt Status: DEP SDC

Copies To: Chaitanya S Malempati, MD~ DATE OF PROCEDURE: [DOB-82]

PREOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Closed displaced com minuted intraarticular left distal radius fracture.

POSTOPERATIVE DIAGNOSIS: Closed displaced comminuted intraarticular left distal radius fracture.

PROCEDURE: Open reduction and internal fixation of left distal radius using a Stryker distal radius locking plate.

SURGEON: Chaitanya Malempati, D.O.

FIRST ASSISTANT: Nicasio Villarreal Jr., KCSA ANESTHESIA: General.

COMPLICATIONS: None.

ESTIMATED BLOOD LOSS: Less than 5 mL. TOURNIQUET TIME: 40 minutes.

INDICATION: The patient is a pleasant 33-year-old female who sustained a fall and had left distal radius fracture. Failed non-operative modalities. | reviewed

imaging with the patient. She elected to proceed with ORIF procedure. All

surgical and non-surgical options with risks, benefits, potential complications,

and outcomes were discussed in length with the patient. She understood and all questions were answered. She did sign consents for the procedure and blood products and agreed to proceed with the procedure.

DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: The procedure was discussed between the operative surgeon and the patient in the preoperative area. They both agreed to proceed with

the procedure and signed consents for the procedure and blood products. The left

upper extremity was marked. The patient was brought back to the operative suite, transferred from the gurney to the operating room table and positioned

appropriately for the procedure. A surgical time-out was performed with the

operative surgeon in the room. General anesthesia was administered per Anesthesiolagy. The left upper extremity was prepped and draped in the appropriate sterile fashion. An Esmarch was used to exsanguinate the limb and tourniquet was inflated to 250 mmHg.

| made a volar FCR approach with a #15 blade scalpel through the skin, subcutaneous

Health Information Management 1208-01664




BGM Patient name: Hall,Cora Mae Account #: L00039407077

tissue, and subcutaneous fat and continued dissection was performed very carefully. | retracted the FCR tendon appropriately. | then accessed the fracture site,

cleaned out using a curette and copiously irrigated using normal saline. |

performed a reduction maneuver with a Freer. Once found to be reduced in the AP, lateral, and fluoroscopic views, | placed a Stryker distal radius locking plate.

Three proximal cortical screws and seven distal locking screws were placed. Final images were taken showing good reduction of the fracture and goad positioning of plate and screws. Copious irrigation was performed. 0 Vicryl suture for deep tissue, 2-0 Vicryl for subcutaneous tissue and 3-0 nylon suture on the skin.

Cleaned and dried appropriately. Dressed using Xeroform, 4x4's, ABDs, Sof-Rol, and a well-padded volar plaster splint. Drapes were removed. Tourniquet was deflated. The patient was transferred from the operating table to the gurney and to the PACU for recovery. There were no complications from anesthesia at any portion of the procedure.

DISPOSITION: She will be discharged home from the PACU once stable. All discharge instructions will be given to the patient at discharge including pain medication

and nausea medication scripts. The patient will be non-weightbearing on left upper extremity. Follow up in postoperative clinic in two weeks. Keep the splint on and

clean, dry and intact. Antibiotics for infection prophylaxis.

Physician Instructions: eee. Instruct patients who are presently on thyroid, seizure, steroid, heart, blood pressure (except ACE inhibitors), or breathing medication to take these medications as routine on the morning of surgery With 15 ml or less of water immediately upon awakenmg; they are not to take any medications other than these until after surgery. ***

five days prior to surgery. ***

*Live* Commonwealth Health Cor Patient Order Summary Page: 22 of 43 Date: 12/20/22 04:04 User: Hopkins, Katrina L L00039407077 Hall,Cora Mae Location: BGM Ambulatory Surgery Medical Record Number: L000617236 33/F Attending: Malempati,Chaitanya 8S, DO Account Number: LO00039407077 Reason: ORIF of Left Distal Radius Registration: 12/08/22

Category Order Ord Provider Entered By

Protocol text: For patients with a history af diabetes or blood glucose greater than 180 mg/dL: 1. Accu-chek every 2 hours while in pre-op and post-op recovery areas 2. If insulin is given, check blood glucase prior to discharge 3. Prior to surgery, notify the anesthesiologist of the DOSE and TIME insulin is given. 4. Use Insulin-Sensitive Protocol for patients with any of the following: - Age over 70 years - Chronic renal insufficiency or creatinine greater than 1.5 mg/dL - History of more than one episode of hypoglycemia in 3 months Follow hypoglycemia protocal for blood sugar less than 70 * Call MD if used * Tf alert, juice or a light snack (only if patient is post-operative) * Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with juice or light snack every 15 minutes until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL * If unable to take PO and IV in place: 1 syringe D50 (25 GM)

* Repeat Accu-chek and retreat with 1 syringe of D5S0 every 15 minutes

until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL

* If unable to take PO and no IV in place: Glucagon Img IM and start IV * If no response by the time IV is started, give 1 syringe of DS50 (25 GM) every 15 minutes until blood sugar is greater than 70 mg/dL Dose Intruction: Perioperative Humalog Sliding Scale while in pre-op and post-op recovery areas:

BS 0-190 = NO INSULIN

BS 181-220 = 3 UNITS (2 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

BS 221-260 4 UNITS (3 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

BS 261-300 6 UNITS (4 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

BS 301-350 8 UNITS (5 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

BS 351-400 10 UNITS (6 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

BS >400 = UNITS (8 UNITS IF INSULIN-SENSITIVE)

Initiate Sleep Apnea Orders

+ Protocol

Stop Reason: Discharged

Physician Instructions:

Continued on Next Page

FOR PATIENTS WITH DIAGNOSED OSA REQUIRING HOME PAP/SUPPLEMENTAL OXYGEN OR HIGH RISK OSA PATIENTS (SBAT>3)

-Initiate and titrate PAP therapy signs of the following (DO NOT USE FOR UPPER AIRWAY, PROCEDURES) :

*Obstruction,

(home setting or 8-12 cm H20) NASAL,

if patient shows OR BARIATRIC

episodes of apnea, (<92%)

and loud snoring *Low oxygen saturations that cannot be resolved with oxygen and use of oral or nasal airway

*Difficulty arousing patient, maintaining eye or verbal contact

-Place patient in non-supine position throughout recovery process if feasible. -If oxygen saturation persistently <88% on oxygen support and/or change in level of consciousness (LOC) please call RT to obtain ABG and contact anesthesia.

-Patients having airway surgery (i.e UPPP), upper abdominal surgery, or

tonsillectomy (age <3) must be admitted post-operatively.

-If patient requiring PAP support or supplemental oxygen after one hour of PACU time,

please contact anesthesia for in-person assessment/sign-out.

-If patient requires CPAP at any point during PACU stay, please place continuous oxygen therapy and standard monitoring including pulse oximetry in Phase 2 recovery area until patient is ambulatory or can maintain room air Sa02 >90%.

-If at risk patient has episode of axygen desaturation that occurs during phase 2 (<90%),

anesthesia.

recovery additional hour must be added to recovery time. Please notify -Patient must be able to maintain baseline 02 saturations on room air for >30 min prior ta Phase 2 discharge.

-Outpatient surgery patients are required to have adult supervision at home for 24

hours past-operatively.

Kugma,Adam, CRNA

The doctor has explained to me: (1) the nature, purpose, description and benefits of the operation, special procedure or treatment; (2) the possibility that complications may arise or develop during the procedure or treatment or recuperation period, and the risks which may be involved; (3) the likelihood of achieving treatment goals; and (4) the possible alternative methods of treatment, along with the benefits, risks and side effects associated with the alternatives, including not having the procedure or

treatment performed. |

I authorize and direct my doctor(s) and associates or assistants, any healthcare provider or healthcare provider in training and The Medical Center to provide such additional services as they deem necessary, including, but not limited to, the administration or maintenance of anesthesia (including sedation \ analgesia), and the performance of services involving pathology and radiology. I understand medical | services may be performed by physicians or other persons who are not agents or employees of The Medical Center, but are independent contractors, and I may be billed separately for their services.

I understand there are inherent risks with the administration of anesthesia. The doctor, anesthesiologist, | nurse anesthetist or nurse practitioner has explained the risks, benefits and alternative methods of anesthesia. Complications associated with all types of anesthesia include, but are not limited to, damage | to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes, nerves or blood vessels. Drug reactions can occur and may be minor or serious. Very serious complications, including paralysis, brain damage or death are

uncommon, but can occur.

Some procedures may require a transfusion of blood or blood products. I understand a blood transfusion is when blood or blood products are given through a sterile needle into one of my veins. I have been informed of the benefits, alternatives and risks involved in receiving a blood transfusion. The possible risks include, but are not limited to, reactions such as: bruising, swelling, infection or bleeding at the needle site; headache, fever, itching or a rash; volume overload which could affect the heart or lungs;

__ and rarely, transmission of diseases such as HIV, AIDS and hepatitis, which require lengthy treatment and can be fatal. (Although the procedures for screening blood products for diseases such as HIV, AIDS and: hepatitis are effective, no process or testing is 100% reliable.)

Th ] Medical PREOPERATIVE PREGNANCY TESTING Center Education, Consent and/or Refusal of Testing

BOWLING GREEN «SCOTTSWILLE « FRANKLIN

This is to educate female patients within childbearing years undergoing surgery of the potential dangers of anesthesia on a fetus. Exposure to anesthestic agents within the first trimester (first 3 months) of pregnancy may have possible adverse , effects on the fetus.

Studies from the American Society of Anesthesiologists, the Centers for Disease Control and others differ on their analysis & findings. However, studies have shown there may be a possibility of an increase in hydrocephalus (an increase in cerebrospinal fluid in the ventricles of the brain), a possible increase chance of neuro tubal defect (a defect effecting the spinal cord and brain) and other effects (malformations) that can occur when the fetus has been exposed to certain anesthestic agents in the first trimester. Also, there could be spontaneous abortion or possible stillbirth.

Ambulatory Surgery and The Anesthesia Department are providing this information to you so you understand the reasons for pregnancy screening prior to surgery. Initial

CRITERIA FOR TESTING: (Yes to any, requires pregnancy testing, check on Anesthesia orders) ae there any possibility you could be pregnant? Are you experiencing a monthly cycle? ‘ Q) Are you experiencing irregular or missed cycles? QO) Tubal Ligation

CRITERIA FOR NOT TESTING: (Yes to any, requires no pregnancy testing) OQ) >50 years old /no cycle for 12 months OQ Hysterectomy | C} Documented by MD there is no need

I have read this and understand the potential effects anesthesia can have on a fetus. I have answered truthfully the questions above and I hereby, Tall the pregnancy testing. i

CaN

— a8ER OIA

General Conditions of Admission, Consent, Assignment of Benefits & Financial Agreement

Consent to Diagnostic Tests, Procedures and Medical Treatment: Ido voluntarily consent to hospital care involving diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my treating physician(s), practitioner(s) and his or her designees. This consent includes testing for communicable diseases, including but not limited to Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV), hepatitis or any other blood-borne infectious disease if ordered for a diagnostic purpose or due to occupational exposure of a health care worker. I acknowledge no guarantee has been made to me as to the results of examination and treatment in the hospital.

Independent Contractor Acknowledgement:

I understand and acknowledge the physicians and other practitioners involved in my care, including but not limited to my attending physician, consulting physicians, emergency department physicians, physician assistants, nurse practitioners, radiologists, anesthesiologists, nurse anesthetists and pathologists are not agents or employees of The Medical Center. I further understand I will be billed separately for services by these providers. These providers have independent relationships with insurance companies, and the hospital makes no guarantee as to any preferred provider relationships with these physicians/practitioners.

Assignment of Benefits and Financial Agreement:

I certify all information given by me is correct and I accept responsibility for the charges for the care provided. I agree to the assignment of all third-party benefits to The Medical Center and to any physician, practitioner, organization or independent contractor who provided products or services, and agree to pay all charges not covered by

Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice messages and/or automated dialing.

Release of Information:

I authorize the release of all or part of my records, including information stored in The Medical Center corporate-wide database, to my physician(s), whose name I provided at the time of registration, and to any physician or practitioner who has or will provide services to me. I authorize the release of statistical information as required by any local, state or federal agency or managed care program. I authorize the release ‘of my social security number to the manufacturer of any implantable medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act of the FDA. I authorize the release of my HIV and hepatitis test results to health care personnel in the event of an occupational exposure.

I authorize the hospital, physicians and any other holder of medical or

other information to release any information about me (including medical information concerning psychological or psychiatric conditions,

alcoholism and/or drug related conditions and HIV or other blood-bome infectious diseases) required for the completion of any claim for benefits arising out of services rendered to me either on an inpatient or outpatient basis to any person or corporation which is or may be liable for all or part of the total charge incurred, including but not limited to insurance companies, the Social Security Administration, its intermediaries and carriers, state agencies and workers’ compensation carriers, as well as the review organization employed by my employer or the employer of the insured member of my family and any corporation engaged by the hospital to make collection of any unpaid hospital charges. I further authorize my employer to

third-party payers. If 1 am covered by an ERISA plan, with this assignment release to the hospital or any agency engaged for the purpose of collecting

I specifically authorize my providers to receive copies of all notifications and information that I am legally entitled to receive under the terms of my insurance/health plan and to act on my behalf to appeal benefit determinations. I acknowledge any claim for benefits from a third party payer may be filed by The Medical Center as a courtesy to me. However, Tam primarily responsible for monitoring the filing process and making

certain the claim is filed in compliance with the provisions specified by. the evaluated as part of this pro; applicable third party payer. The filing of the claim by The Medical Center performance. I understand

in no way absolves me from liability for any portion of the bill not paid by a third party payer for any reason. In the case of outpatient services, I agree this document shall remain in full force and effect until specifically tevoked by me in writing. This writing is intended to be the complete and exclusive statement of the terms and conditions regarding my assignment of benefits and supersedes all previous communications, representations or agreements, whether oral or written. Any terms or conditions proposed by me or on my behalf that differ from or are in addition to the terms of this agreement are rejected and shall not become part of this agreement.

Unless other payment arrangements are approved by The Medical Center, the account balance is due upon demand. Failure to remit payment for the services may result in the placement of an account with a collection agency or attomey for collection. All amounts due, as reflected by the final statement and/or amended final statement, shall bear interest from the due date until paid at a per annum rate of eight percent (8%). In the event a claim is reduced to judgment, it shall accrue interest at the judgment rate of six percent (6%) until paid in full. Further, ] agree to pay all costs of collection including court costs, interest, attorney fees and collection agency fees.

Contact Information:

I agree The Medical Center, Commonwealth Health Corporation and their agents, attorneys or collection agencies may contact me regarding medical information or information about my account or for the purposes of collection by telephone at any number provided by me including wireless telephone numbers, and via text messaging or e-mail to any e-mail address provided. Methods of contact may include the use of pre-recorded or artificial voice messages and/or automated dialing.

General Consent to Photograph:

I consent to the taking of pictures, videotapes or other electronic reproductions of my medical or surgical condition or treatment, and the use of the pictures, videotapes or electronic reproductions, for medical treatment or internal or extemal activities, including but not limited to education, research and quality improvement/risk management, all conducted in accordance with The Medical Center's policies. Photographs containing protected health information will be located in the electronic medical record or otherwise securely stored pursuant to approved policies or practices and remain the property of The Medical Center. I understand and agree that no liability of any nature shall be attached to The Medical Center or any other party in acting pursuant to this authorization.

Hall,Cora Mae 07/13/22 Patient Date

The Patient hereby acknowledges and agrees as follows:

1. The Medical Center provides a safe for the protection of patients' valuables (for example, wallet or purse, money, credit cards, driver's license, identification papers, watch, jewelry, etc.). I understand that it is my responsibility to inform a Hospital employee if I have any items that I would like to deposit in the Hospital's safe and, therefore, agree that the Hospital's maximum total liability for the loss of or damage to any of my property placed in the safe is $500.00. I release from liability, indemnify and hold the Hospital, its employees, agents and contractors, harmless from any loss, cost or damage that I sustain because of any damage to or loss of my personal property that may exceed this $500.00 limit.

2. Iunderstand and agree that the Hospital , its employees, agents and contractors, are not responsible for the protection or safekeeping of any items of personal property (for example, personal electronic items, eyeglasses, contact lenses, hearing aids, dentures, etc.) which I keep with me in my hospital room or in any other area of the Hospital. I acknowledge that it is my responsibility to oversee and protect all personal property that remains with me and that I do not provide to the Hospital for deposit into the Hospital's safe. I further release from liability, indemnify and hold the Hospital, its employees, agents and contractors, harmless from loss, cost or damage that I sustain because of any damage to or loss of my personal property that I keep with me during my stay at the Hospital.

ia or ib

Cannot be further subtyped into Type la or Type ib due to high conservation of the 5‘ untranslated region of the HCY genome. In addition. Tyne 6 virus may be misclassified as Type 1 in some cases. The Hepatitis C Virus High-Resolution Genotype by Sequencing test (ARUP test cade 2006999) provides 4 higher level of subtype resolution

INTERPRETIVE INFORMATION: Hepatitis C Genotyping

Hepatitis C Viral RNA is tested using reverse transcription polymerase chain reaction (RT-PCR) to amplify a specific portion of the 5' untranslated region (5‘ UTR) of the viral genome. The amplified nucleic acid is sequenced bi-directionally using dye-terminator chemistry {ABI}. Sequencing data is compared to a database of characterized sequences.

Ieolates of hepatitis C virus are grouped into Six major genotypes (1-6). These genotypes are subtyped according to sequence characteristics. Due to high conservation of the S' untranslated region of the HCV genome. this test has limitations in differentiating subtype la from 1b. Therefore, these subtypes will be reported as la or ib. In rare instances, Type 6 virus nay be misclassified as Type 1. This test was developed and its performance characteristics determined by ARUP Laboratories. It has not been cleared or approved by the US Food and Drug Administration. This test was performed in a CLIA certified laboratory and is intended for clinical purposes.

Performed By: ARUP Laboratories
